## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the rate of change of a population (dP_dt) as a function of time and current population size, which is central to theoretical ecology and population dynamics. The physical relationship typically describes self-limiting growth, density dependence, or time-varying environmental effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unrestricted growth with constant per-capita rate)
- Logistic (Verhulst) differential equation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (self‑limiting growth with carrying capacity 1/c1)
- Gompertz growth model: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) + c2 * P (or equivalently dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(P)) ; decelerating growth with logarithmic self‑limitation)
- Theta‑logistic (Gilpin–Ayala) model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible density‑dependence shape via exponent c2)
- Richards growth equation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized logistic with shape parameter controlling inflection point)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (cubic model with a population threshold below which growth is negative)
- von Bertalanffy growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (allometric growth and linear loss, typical in organism size dynamics)
- Blumberg hyper-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 * (c2 - P)**c3 (asymmetric density dependence)
- Power‑law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (scale‑free density dependence)
- Time‑dependent carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * t)) (linear change of environmental capacity over time)
- Seasonally forced logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (periodic environmental forcing)
- Exponential decay of growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * t) (growth rate declines monotonically with time)
- Time‑dependent growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P / (c1 + c2 * t) (resource depletion slowing growth over time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Self‑limitation (negative density‑dependence): appearance of terms like -c0*P**2 or -c0*P*log(P) indicating competition for resources
- Per‑capita growth separation: the ODE can often be factored as dP_dt = P * f(P) with f(P) a nonlinear function of P
- Carrying capacity concept: model structure contains a factor (K - P) or (1 - P/K) that drives growth to zero at P = K
- Allee effect (positive density‑dependence at low P): a factor (P - A) or a cubic shape causing growth rate to become negative for small P
- Allometric scaling: power‑law exponents on P other than 1, reflecting metabolic or geometric constraints (e.g., P**(2/3) for surface‑area limited growth)
- Gompertzian deceleration: the use of log(P) or P*log(P) signals a slowing growth that never abruptly stops, typical of tumor growth or aging populations
- Non‑autonomous forcing: explicit dependence on t (e.g., sin, exp, algebraic functions of t) indicates environmental variability, seasonality, or resource decay
- Inflection point flexibility: exponents like (1 - (P/K)^theta) adjust the population size at which growth rate peaks, allowing fit to asymmetric S‑shaped curves

- `= P/5.115 - P²/(5.115*34.44) - 1 + P/34.44`

Multiply by `0.845*P`:

Second term: `0.845*(1 - exp(-0.0969*P))*P = 0.845*P - 0.845*P*exp(-0.0969*P)`

Combining:
```
GT = -0.845*P³/(5.115*34.44) + 0.845*P²/5.115 + 0.845*P²/34.44 - 0.845*P + 0.845*P - 0.845*P*exp(-0.0969*P)
```

The `-0.845*P` and `+0.845*P` cancel!

```
GT = -0.845*P³/(176.1) + 0.845*P²*(1/5.115 + 1/34.44) - 0.845*P*exp(-0.0969*P)
```

So: `GT = A*P³ + B*P² - C*P*exp(-D*P)` where A, B, C, D are specific constants.

The rational part: let me do polynomial long division of `c0P²+c3P` by `c1P+c2`:
- `c0P²/(c1P) = (c0/c1)P`
- Remainder: `c0P² + c3P - (c0/c1)P*(c1P+c2) = c0P² + c3P - c0P² - (c0c2/c1)P = (c3 - c0c2/c1)P`
- Next: `(c3-c0c2/c1)P/(c1P) = (c3-c0c2/c1)/c1 = c3/c1 - c0c2/c1²`
- Remainder: `(c3-c0c2/c1)P - (c3/c1-c0c2/c1²)(c1P+c2) = (c3-c0c2/c1)P - (c3-c0c2/c1)P - c2(c3/c1-c0c2/c1²) = -c2(c3c1-c0c2)/c1²`

So: `(c0P²+c3P)/(c1P+c2) = (c0/c1)P + (c3c1-c0c2)/c1² - c2(c3c1-c0c2)/(c1²(c1P+c2))`

This gives: linear in P + constant + 1/(c1P+c2) term. NOT a polynomial. It has a pole at P = -c2/c1.

For GT, we need a polynomial (P³ + P²). A rational function with a pole cannot equal a polynomial. Unless the numerator remainder is zero: `c3c1 - c0c2 = 0`, i.e., `c3 = c0c2/c1`. Actually, I realize I should check candidates more carefully for hidden `P*exp(cP)` terms.

Candidate 76: `P⁴c0*exp(Pc1)*cos(c2t)/(Pc3+c4) + P³c5*exp(Pc1)*cos(c2t)/(Pc3+c4) + P²c6/(Pc3+c4) + Pc7/(Pc3+c4)`

Set c2=0 (cos=1): `(c0P⁴+c5P³)*exp(Pc1)/(c3P+c4) + (c6P²+c7P)/(c3P+c4)`

If c3=0: `(c0P⁴+c5P³)*exp(c1P)/c4 + (c6P²+c7P)/c4`

This gives: `A*P⁴*exp(c1P) + B*P³*exp(c1P) + C*P² + D*P`

GT needs P³ + P² + P*exp(cP). We'd need the exp terms to give P*exp(cP), but we have P⁴*exp and P³*exp. Setting c0=0: `B*P³*exp(c1P) + C*P² + D*P`. Still P³*exp, not P*exp. [NO MATCH]

If c3≠0, the rational function `(c0P⁴+c5P³)*exp(c1P)/(c3P+c4)` — for this to simplify, we'd need c3P+c4 to divide the polynomial part. `P⁴+...` divided by `P+c4/c3` gives P³+... So we'd get `P³*exp(c1P)*...` Still not P*exp. [NO MATCH]

Candidate 120: `P⁴c0*exp(c1t)/(P+c2) + P³c3*exp(c1t)/(P+c2) + P²c4/(P+c2) + Pc5/(P+c2) + Pc6/(P+c2)`

This has exp(c1*t), not exp(cP). Set c0=0, c3=0 to remove t: `(c4P²+(c5+c6)P)/(P+c2)`. Rational function. No exp(cP). [NO MATCH]

Candidate 74: `P²c0/(Pc1+c2) + P²c3*exp(c4t)/(Pc1+c2) + Pc5/(Pc1+c2) + Pc6*exp(c4t)/(Pc1+c2) + c7/(Pc1+c2)`

Set c3=0, c6=0 to remove t: `(c0P²+c5P+c7)/(c1P+c2)`. Rational. No exp(cP). [NO MATCH]

I'm becoming increasingly convinced that NO candidate can match the GT, because the GT requires `P*exp(-αP)` and none of the candidates can produce this term.

But wait — let me reconsider. Maybe I'm wrong about the GT. Let me re-examine.

GT: `0.845*(-1 + P/5.115)*(1 - P/34.44)*P + 0.845*(1 - exp(-0.0969*P))*P`

Let me verify my expansion:
- Term 1: `0.845*(P/5.115 - 1)*(1 - P/34.44)*P`
  
  `(P/5.115 - 1)(1 - P/34.44) = P/5.115 - P²/(5.115*34.44) - 1 + P/34.44`
  
  Multiply by 0.845*P:
  `0.845*[P²/5.115 - P³/(5.115*34.44) - P + P²/34.44]`
  `= 0.845*P²/5.115 + 0.845*P²/34.44 - 0.845*P³/(5.115*34.44) - 0.845*P`

- Term 2: `0.845*P - 0.845*P*exp(-0.0969*P)`

Sum: `0.845*P²/5.115 + 0.845*P²/34.44 - 0.845*P³/(5.115*34.44) - 0.845*P + 0.845*P - 0.845*P*exp(-0.0969*P)`

The -0.845P and +0.845P cancel:
`= 0.845*P²*(1/5.115 + 1/34.44) - 0.845*P³/(5.115*34.44) - 0.845*P*exp(-0.0969*P)`

So GT = `A*P² + B*P³ + C*P*exp(D*P)` where A>0, B<0, C<0, D<0.

This confirms: the GT requires {P², P³, P*exp(negative*P)} as basis functions.

Now, I need to find candidates that can produce ALL THREE of these.

The critical missing piece in almost all candidates is `P*exp(cP)`.

Let me check one more time if any candidate has this:

Going through ALL candidates looking for `exp(c*P)` (not `exp(c*t)`):

- Cand 3: `exp(Pc6)` — yes, but multiplied by sin(c7t+c8). If c7=0: const*exp(Pc6). Not P*exp.
- Cand 6: inside log — softplus
- Cand 8: inside log — softplus  
- Cand 48: `c5*exp(Pc6)` — exp(cP), not P*exp(cP)
- Cand 62: `c2*exp(Pc3)` — same
- Cand 66: inside log — softplus
- Cand 75: `c4*exp(Pc5)*sin(c6t+c7)` — if c6=0: const*exp(Pc5)
- Cand 76: `P^n*exp(Pc1)*cos(c2t)` — P^4 or P^3 times exp, not P*exp
- Cand 80: `P^c4*exp(Pc6)*cos(c7t)` — if c4=1, c7=0: P*exp(Pc6)! ✓
- Cand 129: inside log — softplus

So only Candidate 80 has `P*exp(cP)`, but as I showed above, its other terms can only produce linear+constant (not P³+P²).

Actually wait, let me reconsider Candidate 80 with c1≠0.

`P²c0/(Pc1+c2) + Pc3/(Pc1+c2) + c5*P*exp(c6P)`

The rational part is `(c0P²+c3P)/(c1P+c2)`. This is a rational function, not a polynomial. For it to equal `A*P² + B*P³`, we'd need:

`(c0P²+c3P)/(c1P+c2) = B*P³ + A*P²`

`c0P²+c3P = (B*P³+A*P²)(c1P+c2) = Bc1*P⁴ + (Bc2+Ac1)*P³ + Ac2*P²`

Comparing: Bc1=0, Bc2+Ac1=0, Ac2=c0, 0=c3.

From Bc1=0: either B=0 or c1=0.
If c1=0: `c0P²/c2 + c3P/c2` = quadratic + linear. Not cubic.
If B=0: then Ac1=0, so A=0 or c1=0. If A=0: everything is 0. If c1=0: back to previous case.

So the rational part CANNOT produce P³. [NO MATCH] confirmed for Candidate 80.

Is there any other way? What about Candidate 76 with different parameter choices?

Candidate 76: `P⁴c0*exp(Pc1)*cos(c2t)/(Pc3+c4) + P³c5*exp(Pc1)*cos(c2t)/(Pc3+c4) + P²c6/(Pc3+c4) + Pc7/(Pc3+c4)`

Set c2=0: `[(c0P⁴+c5P³)*exp(c1P) + c6P²+c7P]/(c3P+c4)`

For this to equal `AP³ + BP² + CP*exp(DP)`:

`(c0P⁴+c5P³)*exp(c1P) + c6P²+c7P = (AP³+BP²+CP*exp(DP))*(c3P+c4)`

RHS = `Ac3P⁴ + (Ac4+Bc3)P³ + Bc4P² + Cc3P²*exp(DP) + Cc4P*exp(DP)`

Comparing exp terms: `(c0P⁴+c5P³)*exp(c1P) = (Cc3P²+Cc4P)*exp(DP)`

This requires c1=D and `c0P⁴+c5P³ = Cc3P²+Cc4P`, which is impossible (degree mismatch). [NO MATCH]

I'm now quite confident that NO candidate can exactly match the GT.

But let me double-check by considering whether the GT could be rewritten in a form that matches some candidate. 

Could `P*exp(-αP)` be expressed as a combination of `sin`, `log`, rational functions, or power laws? No — these are fundamentally different analytic functions. `exp(-αP)` is an entire function with a specific Taylor series that cannot be reproduced by any finite combination of polynomials, logs, sins, or rational functions.

However, let me reconsider one more time. What about:

Candidate 129: `Pc0 + c1*log(Pc2+1) + c3*log(c4*exp(Pc5)+1)`

The term `log(c4*exp(Pc5)+1)`:
- If c4 > 0, c5 < 0: for large P, exp(c5P) → 0, so log(c4*0+1) = 0. For P=0: log(c4+1).
- This is a softplus-like function. Its derivative is `c5*c4*exp(c5P)/(c4*exp(c5P)+1)`.

This is NOT equal to P*exp(-αP). The softplus function approaches 0 for large P (when c5<0) and log(c4+1) for P=0, while P*exp(-αP) approaches 0 for large P and 0 for P=0. But their functional forms are different. Specifically, softplus is monotonic while P*exp(-αP) has a maximum. [NO MATCH]

What about Candidate 82: `Pc0 + P*c1*log(Pc2+1) + P^c3*c4*(-P+c5)^c6`

The term `P^c3*(-P+c5)^c6` — this is a product of power functions. For P ≥ 0 and P < c5, this is well-defined. But this is a power-law expression, not exponential. It cannot equal P*exp(-αP) for all P. [NO MATCH]

Candidate 84: `P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2*(1-(Pc3)^c4)^c5`

The term `P*(1-(c3P)^c4)^c5` — this is a power-law expression. Not exp. [NO MATCH]

Candidate 88: `Pc0 + P^c1*c2*(-P+c3)^c4 + c5*log(Pc6+1)`

`P^c1*(-P+c3)^c4` — power law product. Not exp. [NO MATCH]

Candidate 19: `Pc0 + P^c1*c2 + P^c3*c4*(-P+c5)^c6 + c7*t^c8`

Set c7=0. `Pc0 + P^c1*c2 + P^c3*c4*(-P+c5)^c6`. Power laws. Not exp. [NO MATCH]

Candidate 131: `Pc0 + Pc1 + P^c2*c3 + P^c4*c5` — pure power laws. [NO MATCH]
Candidate 132: `Pc0 + P^c1*c2 + P^c3*c4` — pure power laws. [NO MATCH]
